2976

2977 <section id="_29">

2978

2979 <h2>

2980Treatment of Localized Osteosarcoma and UPS of Bone</h2>

2981

2982 <div id="_section_29" class="pdq-sections">

2983<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

2984<h6>

2985In This Section</h6>

2986<ul>

2987<li>

2988<a href="#_1887_toc">

2989Treatment Options for Localized Osteosarcoma and UPS of Bone<ul>

2990<li>

2991<a href="#_248_toc">

2992Surgical removal of primary tumor</a>

2993</li>

2994<li>

2995<a href="#_252_toc">

2996Chemotherapy</a>

2997</li>

2998<li>

2999<a href="#_1829_toc">

3000Radiation therapy</a>

3001</li>

3002</ul>

3003</a>

3004</li>

3005<li>

3006<a href="#_321_toc">

3007Osteosarcoma of the Head and Neck</a>

3008</li>

3009<li>

3010<a href="#_TrialSearch_29_sid_7_toc">

3011Current Clinical Trials</a>

3012</li>

3013</ul>

3014</nav>

3015<p id="_30" tabindex="-1">

3016Patients with localized osteosarcoma who undergo surgery and chemotherapy have a 5-year overall survival (OS) rate of 62% to 65%.[<a href="#cit/section_7.1">

30171</a>

3018] Complete surgical resection is crucial for patients with localized osteosarcoma; however, at least 80% of patients treated with surgery alone will develop metastatic disease.[<a href="#cit/section_7.2">

30192</a>

3020] Randomized clinical trials have established that adjuvant chemotherapy is

3021effective in preventing relapse or recurrence in patients with localized

3022resectable primary tumors.[<a href="#cit/section_7.2">

30232</a>

3024]; [<a href="#cit/section_7.3">

30253</a>

3026][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3027Level of evidence A1</a>

3028] </p>

3029<p id="_355" tabindex="-1">

3030Undifferentiated pleomorphic sarcoma (UPS) of bone is seen more commonly in older adults. Patients with UPS of bone are treated according to osteosarcoma treatment protocols, and the outcome for patients with resectable UPS is similar to the outcome for patients with osteosarcoma.[<a href="#cit/section_7.4">

30314</a>

3032] As with osteosarcoma, patients with favorable necrosis (&#8805;90% necrosis) have a longer survival than do those with an inferior necrosis (&lt;90% necrosis).[<a href="#cit/section_7.5">

30335</a>

3034] Many patients with UPS will need preoperative chemotherapy to achieve a wide local excision.[<a href="#cit/section_7.6">

30356</a>

3036]</p>

3037<section id="_1887">

3038<h3 id="_1887_toc">

3039Treatment Options for Localized Osteosarcoma and UPS of Bone</h3>

3040<p id="_1823" tabindex="-1">

3041Treatment options for patients with localized osteosarcoma or UPS of bone include the following:</p>

3042<div class="pdq-content-list">

3043<ol id="_1824">

3044<li>

3045<a href="/types/bone/hp/osteosarcoma-treatment-pdq#_248">

3046Surgical removal of primary tumor</a>

3047.</li>

3048<li>

3049<a href="/types/bone/hp/osteosarcoma-treatment-pdq#_252">

3050Chemotherapy</a>

3051 (may start before or after definitive surgical resection of the primary tumor).</li>

3052<li>

3053<a href="/types/bone/hp/osteosarcoma-treatment-pdq#_1829">

3054Radiation therapy, if surgery is not feasible or surgical margins are inadequate</a>

3055.</li>

3056</ol>

3057</div>

3058<section id="_248">

3059<h4 id="_248_toc">

3060Surgical removal of primary tumor</h4>

3061<p id="_249" tabindex="-1">

3062Surgical resection of the primary tumor with adequate margins is an essential component of the curative strategy for patients with localized osteosarcoma. The type of surgery required for complete ablation of the primary tumor depends on a number of factors that must be evaluated on a case-by-case basis.[<a href="#cit/section_7.7">

30637</a>

3064]</p>

3065<section id="_1950">

3066<h5 id="_1950_toc">

3067Limb-sparing procedures</h5>

3068<p id="_356" tabindex="-1">

3069In general, more than 80% of patients with extremity osteosarcoma can be treated using a limb-sparing procedure and do not require amputation.[<a href="#cit/section_7.8">

30708</a>

3071] Limb-sparing procedures are planned only when the preoperative staging indicates that it would be possible to achieve wide surgical margins. In one study, patients who underwent limb-salvage procedures who had poor histologic response and close surgical margins had a high rate of local recurrence.[<a href="#cit/section_7.9">

30729</a>

3073] </p>

3074<p id="_1825" tabindex="-1">

3075Reconstruction after limb-sparing surgery can be accomplished with many options, including metallic endoprosthesis, allograft, vascularized autologous bone graft, and rotationplasty. An additional option, osteogenesis distraction bone transport, is available for patients whose tumors do not involve the epiphysis of long bones.[<a href="#cit/section_7.10">

307610</a>

3077] This procedure results in a stable reconstruction that functionally restores the normal limb. </p>

3078<p id="_1826" tabindex="-1">

3079The choice of optimal surgical reconstruction involves many factors, including the following:[<a href="#cit/section_7.11">

308011</a>

3081][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3082Level of evidence A1</a>

3083]</p>

3084<div class="pdq-content-list">

3085<ul id="_1827">

3086<li>

3087Site and size of the primary tumor.</li>

3088<li>

3089Ability to preserve the neurovascular supply of the distal extremity.</li>

3090<li>

3091Age of the patient and potential for additional growth.</li>

3092<li>

3093Needs and desires of the patient and family for specific functions such as sports participation. </li>

3094</ul>

3095</div>

3096<p id="_1828" tabindex="-1">

3097If a complicated reconstruction delays or prohibits the resumption of systemic chemotherapy, limb preservation may endanger the chance for cure. In retrospective analyses of 703 patients with localized osteosarcoma, the resumption of chemotherapy 21 days or more after definitive surgery was associated with an increased risk of death and adverse events (hazard ratio [HR], 1.57; 1.04&#8211;2.36).[<a href="#cit/section_7.11">

309811</a>

3099] Delays in total time to completion of chemotherapy have also been associated with inferior OS and event-free survival (EFS). In a retrospective multivariate analysis of 113 patients with localized osteosarcoma, a delay of time to completion of chemotherapy greater than 4 weeks was associated with an OS HR of 2.70 (1.11&#8211;6.76, <em>

3100P</em>

3101 = .003) and an EFS HR of 1.13 (1.00&#8211;1.26, <em>

3102P</em>

3103 = .016).[<a href="#cit/section_7.12">

310412</a>

3105]</p>

3106</section>

3107<section id="_1951">

3108<h5 id="_1951_toc">

3109Amputation</h5>

3110<p id="_357" tabindex="-1">

3111For some patients, amputation remains the optimal choice for management of the primary tumor. A pathological fracture noted at diagnosis or during preoperative chemotherapy does not preclude limb-salvage surgery if wide surgical margins can be achieved.[<a href="#cit/section_7.13">

311213</a>

3113] If the pathological examination of the surgical specimen shows inadequate margins, an immediate amputation should be considered, especially if the histologic necrosis after preoperative chemotherapy was poor.[<a href="#cit/section_7.14">

311414</a>

3115]</p>

3116</section>

3117<section id="_1952">

3118<h5 id="_1952_toc">

3119Factors associated with an increased risk of local recurrence</h5>

3120<p id="_250" tabindex="-1">

3121Patients who undergo amputation have lower local recurrence rates than do patients who undergo limb-salvage procedures.[<a href="#cit/section_7.15">

312215</a>

3123] There is no difference in OS between patients initially treated with amputation and those treated with a limb-sparing procedure.

3124Patients with tumors of the femur have a higher local recurrence rate than do patients with primary tumors of the tibia or fibula. Rotationplasty and other limb-salvage procedures have been evaluated for both their functional outcome and their effect on survival. While limb-sparing resection is the current practice for local control at most pediatric institutions, there are few data to indicate that salvage of the lower limb is substantially superior to amputation with regard to patient quality of life.[<a href="#cit/section_7.16">

312516</a>

3126]</p>

3127<p id="_343" tabindex="-1">

3128The German Cooperative Osteosarcoma Study Group performed a retrospective analysis of 1,802 patients with localized and metastatic osteosarcoma who underwent surgical resection of all clinically detectable disease.[<a href="#cit/section_7.17">

312917</a>

3130][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3131Level of evidence C1</a>

3132] Local recurrence (n = 76) was associated with a high risk of death from osteosarcoma. Factors associated with an increased risk of local recurrence included nonparticipation in a clinical trial, pelvic primary site, limb-preserving surgery, soft tissue infiltration beyond the periosteum, poor pathological response to initial chemotherapy, failure to complete planned chemotherapy, and performing the biopsy at an institution different from where the definitive surgery is being performed.</p>

3133</section>

3134</section>

3135<section id="_252">

3136<h4 id="_252_toc">

3137Chemotherapy</h4>

3138<section id="_1830">

3139<h5 id="_1830_toc">

3140Preoperative chemotherapy</h5>

3141<p id="_253" tabindex="-1">

3142Almost all patients receive intravenous preoperative chemotherapy as initial treatment. However, a standard chemotherapy regimen has not been determined. Current chemotherapy protocols

3143include combinations of the following agents: high-dose methotrexate,

3144doxorubicin, cyclophosphamide, cisplatin, ifosfamide, etoposide, and

3145carboplatin.[<a href="#cit/section_7.18">

314618</a>

3147-<a href="#cit/section_7.26">

314826</a>

3149]</p>

3150<p id="_1831" tabindex="-1">

3151Evidence (preoperative chemotherapy):</p>

3152<div class="pdq-content-list">

3153<ol id="_1832">

3154<li>

3155 A meta-analysis of protocols for the treatment of osteosarcoma concluded the following:[<a href="#cit/section_7.27">

315627</a>

3157]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3158<ul id="_1888">

3159<li>

3160Regimens containing three active chemotherapy agents were superior to regimens containing two active agents.</li>

3161<li>

3162Regimens with four active agents were not superior to regimens with three active agents.</li>

3163<li>

3164Three-drug regimens that did not include high-dose methotrexate were inferior to three-drug regimens that did include high-dose methotrexate.</li>

3165</ul>

3166</div>

3167</li>

3168<li>

3169An Italian study that used regimens containing fewer courses of high-dose methotrexate observed the following results:[<a href="#cit/section_7.28">

317028</a>

3171][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3172Level of evidence B4</a>

3173]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3174<ul id="_1942">

3175<li>

3176There was a lower probability for EFS than found in earlier studies that used regimens containing more courses of high-dose methotrexate.</li>

3177</ul>

3178</div>

3179</li>

3180<li>

3181The Children's Oncology Group (COG) performed a prospective randomized trial in newly diagnosed children and young adults with localized osteosarcoma. All patients received cisplatin, doxorubicin, and high-dose methotrexate. One-half of the patients were randomly assigned to receive ifosfamide. In a second randomization, one-half of the patients were assigned to receive the biological compound muramyl tripeptide-phosphatidyl ethanolamine encapsulated in liposomes (L-MTP-PE) beginning after definitive surgical resection. Results showed that:[<a href="#cit/section_7.29">

318229</a>

3183][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3184Level of evidence A1</a>

3185]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3186<ul id="_1833">

3187<li>

3188 The addition of ifosfamide did not improve outcome.</li>

3189<li>

3190The addition of L-MTP-PE produced improvement in the EFS rate, which did not meet the conventional test for statistical significance (<em>

3191P</em>

3192 = .08), and a significant improvement in the OS rate (78% vs. 70%; <em>

3193P</em>

3194 = .03).</li>

3195<li>

3196There has been speculation regarding the potential contribution of postrelapse treatment, although there were no differences in the postrelapse surgical approaches in the relapsed patients. The appropriate role of L-MTP-PE in the treatment of osteosarcoma remains under discussion.[<a href="#cit/section_7.30">

319730</a>

3198]</li>

3199</ul>

3200</div>

3201</li>

3202<li>

3203The COG performed a series of pilot studies in patients with newly diagnosed localized osteosarcoma.[<a href="#cit/section_7.31">

320431</a>

3205][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3206Level of evidence B4</a>

3207] <div class="pdq-content-list">

3208<ol id="_1834" class="lower-alpha">

3209<li>

3210In pilot study 1, patients with lower degrees of necrosis after three-drug initial therapy received subsequent therapy with a higher cumulative dose of doxorubicin of 600 mg/m<span class="sup">

32112</span>

3212. </li>

3213<li>

3214In pilot study 2, all patients received four-drug initial chemotherapy with cisplatin, doxorubicin, high-dose methotrexate, and ifosfamide. Patients with lower degrees of necrosis received subsequent chemotherapy with a higher cumulative dose of doxorubicin of 600 mg/m<span class="sup">

32152</span>

3216. </li>

3217<li>

3218In pilot study 3, all patients received the same four-drug initial chemotherapy as pilot study 2. Patients with lower degrees of necrosis received higher doses of ifosfamide with the addition of etoposide in subsequent therapy.</li>

3219</ol>

3220</div>

3221<p id="_1953" tabindex="-1">

3222The results of these pilot studies were as follows:</p>

3223<div class="pdq-content-list">

3224<ul id="_1835">

3225<li>

3226Outcomes for all three pilot studies were similar to each other and to historical controls. </li>

3227<li>

3228All patients received dexrazoxane before each dose of doxorubicin. The addition of dexrazoxane did not appear to decrease the rate of good necrosis after initial therapy or EFS.</li>

3229<li>

3230Left ventricular fractional shortening, as measured by echocardiography, was minimally affected at 78 weeks from study entry.</li>

3231<li>

3232There was no evidence for an increased risk of secondary leukemia.</li>

3233</ul>

3234</div>

3235</li>

3236<li>

3237The international European and American Osteosarcoma Study (EURAMOS) Group consortium was formed to conduct a large, prospective, randomized trial to help determine whether modifying the chemotherapy regimen on the basis of the degree of necrosis would improve EFS. All patients received initial therapy with cisplatin, doxorubicin, and high-dose methotrexate (MAP). Patients with more than 90% necrosis were randomly assigned to continue the same chemotherapy after surgery or to receive the same chemotherapy with the addition of interferon alpha-2B. Patients with less than 90% necrosis were randomly assigned to continue the same chemotherapy or to receive the same chemotherapy with the addition of high-dose ifosfamide and etoposide (MAPIE).[<a href="#cit/section_7.32">

323832</a>

3239][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3240Level of evidence A1</a>

3241]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3242<ul id="_1927">

3243<li>

3244 At a median follow-up of 54 months for all registered patients (N = 2,260), the 3-year EFS rate was 59% (95% confidence interval [CI], 57%&#8211;61%), and the 5-year EFS rate was 54% (95% CI, 52%&#8211;56%).</li>

3245<li>

3246 The 3-year OS rate was 79% (95% CI, 77%&#8211;81%), and the 5-year OS rate was 71% (95% CI, 68%&#8211;73%).</li>

3247<li>

3248 Patients with localized disease at diagnosis (M0) who underwent complete surgical resection (n = 1,549) had 3-year EFS and OS rates from surgery of 70% and 88%, respectively; the 5-year EFS and OS rates from surgery were 64% and 79%, respectively.</li>

3249<li>

3250Forty percent of patients/families who participated in the study declined randomization after definitive surgical resection, making interpretation of the outcome of the randomized study questions more difficult and challenging the generalizability of the results.</li>

3251<li>

3252Of patients with more than 90% necrosis, 716 were randomly assigned to continue the same chemotherapy after surgery with or without the addition of interferon alpha-2B. The 3-year EFS rates were 74% (95% CI, 69%&#8211;79%) for patients who received MAP and 77% (95% CI, 72%&#8211;81%) for patients who received MAP plus interferon alpha-2B. The HR was 0.83 (95% CI, 0.61&#8211;1.12; <em>

3253P</em>

3254 = .2).[<a href="#cit/section_7.33">

325533</a>

3256]</li>

3257<li>

3258Of patients with less than 90% necrosis, 618 were randomly assigned to continue MAP chemotherapy or to receive MAPIE chemotherapy. The 3-year EFS estimates for patients with localized disease were 60% (95% CI, 54%&#8211;66%) for the MAP group and 57% (95% CI, 51%&#8211;63%) for the MAPIE group. The HR was 1.03 (0.81&#8211;1.33, <em>

3259P</em>

3260 = .80).[<a href="#cit/section_7.34">

326134</a>

3262]</li>

3263</ul>

3264</div>

3265</li>

3266</ol>

3267</div>

3268</section>

3269<section id="_1836">

3270<h5 id="_1836_toc">

3271Postoperative chemotherapy</h5>

3272<p id="_535" tabindex="-1">

3273Historically, the extent of tumor necrosis was used in some clinical trials to determine what type of postoperative chemotherapy would be given. In general, if tumor necrosis exceeded 90%, the preoperative chemotherapy regimen was continued. If tumor necrosis was less than 90%, some groups incorporated drugs not previously utilized in the preoperative therapy.</p>

3274<p id="_511" tabindex="-1">

3275Patients with less necrosis after initial chemotherapy have a prognosis that is inferior to the prognosis for patients with more necrosis. The prognosis is still substantially better than the prognosis for patients treated with surgery alone and no adjuvant chemotherapy. </p>

3276<p id="_1954" tabindex="-1">

3277Based on the following evidence, it is inappropriate to conclude that patients with less necrosis have not responded to chemotherapy and that adjuvant chemotherapy should be withheld for these patients. Chemotherapy after definitive surgery should include the agents used in the initial phase of treatment unless there is clear and unequivocal progressive disease during the initial phase of therapy.</p>

3278<p id="_1837" tabindex="-1">

3279Evidence (using the same agents for postoperative chemotherapy):</p>

3280<div class="pdq-content-list">

3281<ol id="_1838">

3282<li>

3283Early reports from the Memorial Sloan Kettering Cancer Center (MSKCC) that suggested that adding cisplatin to postoperative chemotherapy improved the outcome for patients with less than 90% tumor necrosis.[<a href="#cit/section_7.35">

328435</a>

3285] <div class="pdq-content-list">

3286<ul id="_1955">

3287<li>

3288With longer follow-up, the outcome for patients with less than 90% tumor necrosis treated at MSKCC was the same whether they did or did not receive cisplatin in the postoperative phase of treatment.[<a href="#cit/section_7.36">

328936</a>

3290]</li>

3291</ul>

3292</div>

3293</li>

3294<li>

3295In an early experience, the German cooperative osteosarcoma group performed a trial in which the chemotherapy regimen for patients with poor necrosis was changed after initial treatment.[<a href="#cit/section_7.37">

329637</a>

3297] The agents used before surgery were discontinued and other agents were substituted. <div class="pdq-content-list">

3298<ul id="_1839">

3299<li>

3300The results were substantially poorer for these patients than for patients who continued to receive the same agents.</li>

3301</ul>

3302</div>

3303</li>

3304<li>

3305Subsequent trials performed by other groups failed to demonstrate improved EFS when drugs not included in the preoperative regimen (cisplatin) were added to postoperative therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_7.19">

330619</a>

3307,<a href="#cit/section_7.38">

330838</a>

3309]</li>

3310<li>

3311A limited-institution pilot trial tested the strategy of discontinuing the agents used in the initial phase of therapy for patients with poorer necrosis; postoperative therapy consisted of melphalan with autologous stem cell reconstitution.[<a href="#cit/section_7.39">

331239</a>

3313] <div class="pdq-content-list">

3314<ul id="_1840">

3315<li>

3316The 5-year EFS rate for this group was 28%, which was lower than the EFS rates observed in many large series in which agents were continued despite a lesser degree of necrosis.</li>

3317</ul>

3318</div>

3319</li>

3320<li>

3321The international European and American Osteosarcoma Study (EURAMOS) group consortium was formed to conduct a large, prospective, randomized trial to help determine whether modifying the chemotherapy regimen on the basis of the degree of necrosis would improve EFS. All patients received initial therapy with cisplatin, doxorubicin, and high-dose methotrexate (MAP). Patients with more than 90% necrosis were randomly assigned to continue the same chemotherapy after surgery or to receive the same chemotherapy with the addition of interferon alpha-2b.[<a href="#cit/section_7.33">

332233</a>

3323][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3324Level of evidence B1</a>

3325] In the same EURAMOS trial, patients with less than 90% necrosis were randomly assigned to continue the same chemotherapy or to receive the same chemotherapy with the addition of high-dose ifosfamide and etoposide (MAPIE).[<a href="#cit/section_7.34">

332634</a>

3327][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3328Level of evidence B1</a>

3329]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3330<ul id="_1956">

3331<li>

3332 The addition of interferon alpha-2b did not improve the probability of EFS.</li>

3333<li>

3334With a median follow-up of over 61 months, the EFS did not differ between the two groups. </li>

3335<li>

3336The intensification of treatment in the MAPIE group resulted in greater toxicity than did the treatment in the standard MAP arm.</li>

3337</ul>

3338</div>

3339</li>

3340</ol>

3341</div>

3342</section>

3343<section id="_1843">

3344<h5 id="_1843_toc">

3345Other chemotherapy approaches not considered effective</h5>

3346<p id="_461" tabindex="-1">

3347The Italian Sarcoma Group and the Scandinavian Sarcoma Group performed a clinical trial in patients with osteosarcoma who presented with clinically detectable metastatic disease.[<a href="#cit/section_7.40">

334840</a>

3349] Consolidation with high-dose etoposide and carboplatin followed by autologous stem cell reconstitution did not appear to improve outcome and the investigators did not recommend this strategy for the treatment of osteosarcoma.</p>

3350<p id="_514" tabindex="-1">

3351Laboratory studies using cell lines and xenografts suggested that bisphosphonates had activity against osteosarcoma.[<a href="#cit/section_7.41">

335241</a>

3353] A single-institution clinical trial demonstrated that pamidronate could safely be administered along with multiagent chemotherapy to patients with newly diagnosed osteosarcoma.[<a href="#cit/section_7.41">

335441</a>

3355] The French pediatric and adult sarcoma cooperative groups performed a prospective trial for the treatment of osteosarcoma.[<a href="#cit/section_7.42">

335642</a>

3357] All patients received multiagent chemotherapy, and patients were randomly assigned to receive or not to receive zoledronate. The addition of zoledronate did not improve EFS.</p>

3358</section>

3359</section>

3360<section id="_1829">

3361<h4 id="_1829_toc">

3362Radiation therapy</h4>

3363<p id="_251" tabindex="-1">

3364If complete surgical resection is not feasible or if surgical margins are inadequate, radiation therapy may improve the local control rate.[<a href="#cit/section_7.43">

336543</a>

3366,<a href="#cit/section_7.44">

336744</a>

3368]; [<a href="#cit/section_7.45">

336945</a>

3370][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3371Level of evidence C1</a>

3372] Radiation therapy should be considered in patients with osteosarcoma of the head and neck who have positive or uncertain resection margins.[<a href="#cit/section_7.46">

337346</a>

3374][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3375Level of evidence C1</a>

3376] </p>

3377<p id="_1933" tabindex="-1">

3378Evidence (radiation therapy for local control):</p>

3379<div class="pdq-content-list">

3380<ol id="_1934">

3381<li>

3382While it is accepted that the standard approach is primary surgical resection, a retrospective analysis of a small group of highly selective patients reported long-term EFS with external-beam radiation therapy for local control in some patients.[<a href="#cit/section_7.47">

338347</a>

3384][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3385Level of evidence C1</a>

3386] </li>

3387<li>

3388Investigators from a single institution reported on 28 children and young adults with osteosarcoma who were treated with radiation therapy for local control. Sixteen patients received radiation therapy during the primary treatment course, and 12 patients received radiation therapy as part of therapy after recurrence.[<a href="#cit/section_7.48">

338948</a>

3390]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3391<ul id="_1935">

3392<li>

3393For patients who received radiation therapy during primary treatment, the cumulative incidence of local failure at 5 years was 25%.</li>

3394<li>

3395For patients with recurrent disease, the cumulative incidence of local failure at 5 years was 44%.</li>

3396<li>

3397Local tumor progression was observed in 3 of 13 patients (23%) who were treated with adjuvant radiation therapy after resection, while three of six patients (50%) who received definitive radiation therapy as a sole modality of local control experienced local progression.</li>

3398</ul>

3399</div>

3400</li>

3401</ol>

3402</div>

3403</section>

3404</section>

3405<section id="_321">

3406<h3 id="_321_toc">

3407Osteosarcoma of the Head and Neck</h3>

3408<p id="_322" tabindex="-1">

3409Osteosarcoma of the head and neck occurs in an older population than does osteosarcoma of the extremities.[<a href="#cit/section_7.46">

341046</a>

3411,<a href="#cit/section_7.49">

341249</a>

3413-<a href="#cit/section_7.52">

341452</a>

3415] In the pediatric age group, osteosarcomas of the head and neck are more likely to be low-grade or intermediate-grade tumors than are osteosarcomas of the extremities.[<a href="#cit/section_7.53">

341653</a>

3417,<a href="#cit/section_7.54">

341854</a>

3419] All reported series emphasize the need for complete surgical resection.[<a href="#cit/section_7.46">

342046</a>

3421,<a href="#cit/section_7.49">

342249</a>

3423-<a href="#cit/section_7.54">

342454</a>

3425][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3426Level of evidence C1</a>

3427] The probability for cure with surgery alone is higher for osteosarcoma of the head and neck than it is for extremity osteosarcoma. When surgical margins are positive, there is a trend for improved survival with adjuvant radiation therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_7.46">

342846</a>

3429,<a href="#cit/section_7.51">

343051</a>

3431][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3432Level of evidence C1</a>

3433] </p>

3434<p id="_1844" tabindex="-1">

3435There are no randomized trials to assess the efficacy of chemotherapy in patients with osteosarcoma of the head and neck, but several series suggest a benefit.[<a href="#cit/section_7.49">

343649</a>

3437,<a href="#cit/section_7.55">

343855</a>

3439] Chemotherapy should be considered for younger patients with high-grade osteosarcoma of the head and neck.[<a href="#cit/section_7.53">

344053</a>

3441,<a href="#cit/section_7.56">

344256</a>

3443]</p>

3444<p id="_1845" tabindex="-1">

3445Patients with osteosarcoma of the head and neck have a higher risk of developing a local recurrence and a lower risk of having distant metastasis than do patients with osteosarcoma of the extremities.[<a href="#cit/section_7.49">

344649</a>

3447,<a href="#cit/section_7.51">

344851</a>

3449,<a href="#cit/section_7.52">

345052</a>

3451,<a href="#cit/section_7.57">

345257</a>

3453] </p>

3454</section>

3455<section id="_TrialSearch_29_sid_7">

3456<h3 id="_TrialSearch_29_sid_7_toc">

3457Current Clinical Trials</h3>

3458<p id="_TrialSearch_29_22" tabindex="-1">

3459Use our <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced">

3460advanced clinical trial search</a>

3461 to find NCI-supported cancer clinical trials that are now enrolling patients. The search can be narrowed by location of the trial, type of treatment, name of the drug, and other criteria. <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/">

3462General information</a>

3463 about clinical trials is also available.</p>

3703 <section id="_38">

3704

3705 <h2>

3706Treatment of Osteosarcoma and UPS of Bone With Metastatic Disease at Diagnosis</h2>

3707

3708 <div id="_section_38" class="pdq-sections">

3709<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

3710<h6>

3711In This Section</h6>

3712<ul>

3713<li>

3714<a href="#_1889_toc">

3715Treatment Options for Osteosarcoma and UPS of Bone With Metastatic Disease at Diagnosis</a>

3716</li>

3717<li>

3718<a href="#_256_toc">

3719Treatment Options for Lung-Only Metastases at Diagnosis</a>

3720</li>

3721<li>

3722<a href="#_259_toc">

3723Treatment Options for Bone Metastases With or Without Lung Metastases</a>

3724</li>

3725<li>

3726<a href="#_2402_toc">

3727Treatment Options Under Clinical Evaluation</a>

3728</li>

3729<li>

3730<a href="#_TrialSearch_38_sid_8_toc">

3731Current Clinical Trials</a>

3732</li>

3733</ul>

3734</nav>

3735<p id="_255" tabindex="-1">

3736Approximately 20% to 25% of patients with osteosarcoma present with clinically detectable metastatic disease. For patients with metastatic disease at initial presentation, roughly 20% will remain continuously free of disease, and roughly 30% will survive 5 years from diagnosis.[<a href="#cit/section_8.1">

37371</a>

3738] </p>

3739<p id="_358" tabindex="-1">

3740The lung is the most common site of initial metastatic disease.[<a href="#cit/section_8.2">

37412</a>

3742] Patients with metastases limited to the lungs have a better outcome than do patients with metastases to other sites or to the lungs combined with other sites.[<a href="#cit/section_8.1">

37431</a>

3744,<a href="#cit/section_8.3">

37453</a>

3746]</p>

3747<section id="_1889">

3748<h3 id="_1889_toc">

3749Treatment Options for Osteosarcoma and UPS of Bone With Metastatic Disease at Diagnosis</h3>

3750<p id="_1846" tabindex="-1">

3751Treatment options for patients with osteosarcoma or undifferentiated pleomorphic sarcoma (UPS) of bone with metastatic disease at diagnosis include the following:</p>

3752<div class="pdq-content-list">

3753<ol id="_1847">

3754<li>

3755Chemotherapy.</li>

3756</ol>

3757</div>

3758<p id="_1848" tabindex="-1">

3759The chemotherapeutic agents used include high-dose methotrexate, doxorubicin, cisplatin, high-dose ifosfamide, etoposide, and, in some reports, carboplatin or cyclophosphamide.</p>

3760<p id="_1849" tabindex="-1">

3761Evidence (chemotherapy):</p>

3762<div class="pdq-content-list">

3763<ol id="_1850">

3764<li>

3765In a trial that investigated high-dose ifosfamide (17.5 g per course) in combination with etoposide for patients with newly diagnosed metastatic osteosarcoma, the following was observed:[<a href="#cit/section_8.4">

37664</a>

3767]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3768<ul id="_1957">

3769<li>

3770The combination produced a complete response in 10% of the patients and a partial response in 49% of the patients.</li>

3771</ul>

3772</div>

3773<p id="_1973" tabindex="-1">

3774 However, similar to localized disease, there is no evidence that the addition of ifosfamide or etoposide contributes to improved event-free survival (EFS) or overall survival (OS) in patients with metastatic disease.</p>

3775</li>

3776<li>

3777A study using a factorial design in patients with metastatic osteosarcoma (n = 91) evaluated the addition of either muramyl tripeptide or ifosfamide to a standard chemotherapy regimen that included cisplatin, high-dose methotrexate, and doxorubicin.[<a href="#cit/section_8.5">

37785</a>

3779] <div class="pdq-content-list">

3780<ul id="_1851">

3781<li>

3782There was a nominal advantage for the addition of muramyl tripeptide (but not for ifosfamide) in terms of EFS and OS, but criteria for statistical significance were not met.</li>

3783</ul>

3784</div>

3785</li>

3786<li>

3787In the international European and American Osteosarcoma Study (EURAMOS) group consortium, 362 of 2,186 patients (17%) presented with metastasis at diagnosis. Patients were randomly assigned to receive either treatment with cisplatin, doxorubicin, and high-dose methotrexate or cisplatin, doxorubicin, high-dose methotrexate, and ifosfamide.[<a href="#cit/section_8.6">

37886</a>

3789][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3790Level of evidence A1</a>

3791]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3792<ul id="_1928">

3793<li>

3794 At a median follow-up of 47 months, the 3-year EFS rate was 32% (95% confidence interval [CI], 27%&#8211;37%), and the 5-year EFS rate was 28% (95% CI, 23%&#8211;33%).</li>

3795<li>

3796 The 3-year OS rate was 56% (95% CI, 50%&#8211;61%), and the 5-year OS rate was 45% (95% CI, 39%&#8211;50%). </li>

3797</ul>

3798</div>

3799</li>

3800</ol>

3801</div>

3802<p id="_361" tabindex="-1">

3803The treatment options for UPS of bone with metastasis at initial presentation are the same as the treatment for osteosarcoma with metastasis. Patients with unresectable or metastatic UPS have a very poor outcome.[<a href="#cit/section_8.7">

38047</a>

3805]</p>

3806</section>

3807<section id="_256">

3808<h3 id="_256_toc">

3809Treatment Options for Lung-Only Metastases at Diagnosis</h3>

3810<p id="_1852" tabindex="-1">

3811Treatment options for patients with metastatic lung lesions at diagnosis include the following:</p>

3812<div class="pdq-content-list">

3813<ol id="_1853">

3814<li>

3815Preoperative chemotherapy followed by surgery to remove the tumor followed by postoperative combination chemotherapy.</li>

3816</ol>

3817</div>

3818<p id="_257" tabindex="-1">

3819Patients with metastatic lung lesions as the sole site of metastatic disease should have the lung lesions resected if possible. Generally, this is performed after the administration of preoperative chemotherapy. After definitive surgical resection of the primary tumor, most clinicians resume systemic chemotherapy before initiating lung surgery to avoid longer delays in the resumption of chemotherapy. In approximately 10% of patients, all lung lesions disappear after preoperative chemotherapy.[<a href="#cit/section_8.3">

38203</a>

3821] Complete resection of pulmonary metastatic disease can be achieved in a high percentage of patients with residual lung nodules after preoperative chemotherapy. The long-term survival is poor for patients who do not undergo complete surgical resection of pulmonary metastatic disease.[<a href="#cit/section_8.8">

38228</a>

3823,<a href="#cit/section_8.9">

38249</a>

3825][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3826Level of evidence B4</a>

3827]</p>

3828<p id="_258" tabindex="-1">

3829For patients who present with primary osteosarcoma and metastases limited to the lungs and who achieve complete surgical remission, the 5-year EFS rate is approximately 20% to 25%. Multiple metastatic nodules confer a worse prognosis than do one or two nodules, and bilateral lung involvement is worse than unilateral.[<a href="#cit/section_8.1">

38301</a>

3831] Patients with peripheral lung lesions may have a better prognosis than patients with central lesions.[<a href="#cit/section_8.10">

383210</a>

3833] Patients with fewer than three nodules confined to one lung may achieve a 5-year EFS rate of approximately 40% to 50%.[<a href="#cit/section_8.1">

38341</a>

3835] A multi-institutional retrospective analysis compared thoracotomy with thoracoscopy for resection of pulmonary metastases in patients with osteosarcoma.[<a href="#cit/section_8.11">

383611</a>

3837] The analysis included patients who had pulmonary metastases at diagnosis, patients with pulmonary relapse after initial management of localized disease, and patients with disease progression while on therapy. The authors recognized a significant selection bias for the patients chosen to undergo thoracoscopy. In a Cox regression analysis, controlling for other factors impacting outcome, there was a significantly increased risk of mortality (hazard ratio [HR], 2.11; 95% CI, 1.09&#8211;4.09; <em>

3838P</em>

3839 = .027) but not pulmonary recurrence (HR, 0.96; 95% CI, 0.52&#8211;1.79; <em>

3840P</em>

3841 = .90) with a thoracoscopic approach. In a subset analysis limited to patients with oligometastatic disease, thoracoscopy did not increase the risk of mortality (HR, 1.16; 95% CI, 0.64&#8211;2.11; <em>

3842P</em>

3843 = .62). The ongoing randomized trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT05235165">

3844AOST2031 [NCT05235165]</a>

3845) was designed to definitively address this question and the selection bias. This trial will compare the effect of thoracotomy with thoracoscopic surgery.</p>

3846</section>

3847<section id="_259">

3848<h3 id="_259_toc">

3849Treatment Options for Bone Metastases With or Without Lung Metastases</h3>

3850<p id="_260" tabindex="-1">

3851The second most common site of metastasis is another bone that is distant from the primary tumor. Patients with metastasis to other bones distant from the primary tumor experience EFS and OS rates of approximately 10%.[<a href="#cit/section_8.1">

38521</a>

3853] In a study of patients who presented with primary extremity tumors and synchronous metastasis to other bones, only 3 of 46 patients remained continuously disease-free 5 years later.[<a href="#cit/section_8.12">

385412</a>

3855] Patients with transarticular skip lesions have a poor prognosis.[<a href="#cit/section_8.13">

385613</a>

3857]</p>

3858<p id="_261" tabindex="-1">

3859Multifocal osteosarcoma is different from osteosarcoma that presents with a clearly delineated primary lesion and limited bone metastasis. Multifocal osteosarcoma classically presents with symmetrical, metaphyseal lesions, and it may be difficult to determine the primary lesion. Patients with multifocal bone disease at presentation have an extremely poor prognosis, but treatment with systemic chemotherapy and aggressive surgical resection may significantly prolong life.[<a href="#cit/section_8.14">

386014</a>

3861,<a href="#cit/section_8.15">

386215</a>

3863]</p>

3864<p id="_1854" tabindex="-1">

3865Treatment options for patients with bone metastases with or without lung metastases include the following:</p>

3866<div class="pdq-content-list">

3867<ol id="_1855">

3868<li>

3869Preoperative chemotherapy followed by surgery to remove the primary tumor. After definitive surgical resection of the primary tumor, most clinicians resume systemic chemotherapy. The timing of surgery to remove metastatic tumors is not well defined. It is usually not attempted at the time of primary surgery because delays of more than 21 days until resumption of chemotherapy can increase the risk of adverse events and death.[<a href="#cit/section_8.16">

387016</a>

3871]</li>

3872<li>

3873Surgery to remove the primary tumor followed by chemotherapy and then surgical resection of metastatic disease followed by postoperative combination chemotherapy.<p id="_263" tabindex="-1">

3874 When the usual treatment course of preoperative chemotherapy followed by surgical ablation of the primary tumor and resection of all overt metastatic disease followed by postoperative combination chemotherapy cannot be used, an alternative treatment approach may be used. This alternative treatment approach begins with surgery for the primary tumor, followed by chemotherapy, and then surgical resection of metastatic disease. This approach may be appropriate in patients with intractable pain, pathological fracture, or uncontrolled infection of the tumor when initiation of chemotherapy could create risk of sepsis.[<a href="#cit/section_8.17">

387517</a>

3876]</p>

3877</li>

3878<li>

3879Resection of metastatic bone lesions if possible. </li>

3880<li>

3881Radiation therapy to the extremities. There is some evidence that radiation therapy to the extremities may offer some local control.[<a href="#cit/section_8.18">

388218</a>

3883]</li>

3884</ol>

3885</div>

3886</section>

3887<section id="_2402">

3888<h3 id="_2402_toc">

3889Treatment Options Under Clinical Evaluation</h3>

3890<p id="_503" tabindex="-1">

3891Information about National Cancer Institute (NCI)&#8211;supported clinical trials can be found on the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search">

3892NCI website</a>

3893. For information about clinical trials sponsored by other organizations, see the <a href="https://clinicaltrials.gov/" title="https://clinicaltrials.gov/">

3894ClinicalTrials.gov website</a>

3895.</p>

3896<p id="_1798" tabindex="-1">

3897The following are examples of national and/or institutional clinical trials that are currently being conducted:</p>

3898<div class="pdq-content-list">

3899<ul id="_2403">

3900<li>

3901<strong>

3902<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT05235165">

3903AOST2031 (NCT05235165)</a>

3904</strong>

3905 (Thoracotomy Versus Thoracoscopic Management of Pulmonary Metastases in Patients With Osteosarcoma)<strong>

3906:</strong>

3907 This phase III trial compares the effect of thoracotomy with thoracoscopic surgery (video-assisted thoracoscopic surgery) in treating patients with osteosarcoma that has spread to the lung (pulmonary metastases). This trial is being done to evaluate the two different surgery methods for these patients and to determine which procedure is better.</li>

3908<li>

3909<strong>

3910<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT05691478">

3911AOST2032 (NCT05691478)</a>

3912</strong>

3913 (A Study to Test the Addition of the Drug Cabozantinib to Chemotherapy in Patients With Newly Diagnosed Osteosarcoma)<strong>

3914:</strong>

3915 This trial starts with a feasibility phase for patients with high-risk osteosarcoma who have a resectable primary tumor. The feasibility phase will be followed by a randomized study comparing chemotherapy using methotrexate, doxorubicin, cisplatin (MAP) with MAP and cabozantinib for patients with newly diagnosed localized and metastatic osteosarcoma.</li>

3916</ul>

3917</div>

3918</section>

3919<section id="_TrialSearch_38_sid_8">

3920<h3 id="_TrialSearch_38_sid_8_toc">

3921Current Clinical Trials</h3>

3922<p id="_TrialSearch_38_22" tabindex="-1">

3923Use our <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced">

3924advanced clinical trial search</a>

3925 to find NCI-supported cancer clinical trials that are now enrolling patients. The search can be narrowed by location of the trial, type of treatment, name of the drug, and other criteria. <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/">

3926General information</a>

3927 about clinical trials is also available.</p>

3928</section>
