4012

4013 <h2>

4014Treatment of Recurrent Osteosarcoma and UPS of Bone</h2>

4015

4016 <div id="_section_44" class="pdq-sections">

4017<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

4018<h6>

4019In This Section</h6>

4020<ul>

4021<li>

4022<a href="#_1958_toc">

4023Prognostic Factors for Recurrence</a>

4024</li>

4025<li>

4026<a href="#_1890_toc">

4027Treatment Options for Recurrent Osteosarcoma and UPS of Bone<ul>

4028<li>

4029<a href="#_1943_toc">

4030Surgery</a>

4031</li>

4032<li>

4033<a href="#_1945_toc">

4034Chemotherapy and targeted therapy</a>

4035</li>

4036<li>

4037<a href="#_1946_toc">

4038Radiopharmaceuticals and radiation therapy</a>

4039</li>

4040</ul>

4041</a>

4042</li>

4043<li>

4044<a href="#_275_toc">

4045Treatment Options for Local Recurrence</a>

4046</li>

4047<li>

4048<a href="#_271_toc">

4049Treatment Options for Lung-Only Recurrence</a>

4050</li>

4051<li>

4052<a href="#_273_toc">

4053Treatment Options for Recurrence With Bone-Only Metastases</a>

4054</li>

4055<li>

4056<a href="#_278_toc">

4057Treatment Options for Second Recurrence of Osteosarcoma</a>

4058</li>

4059<li>

4060<a href="#_502_toc">

4061Treatment Options Under Clinical Evaluation<ul>

4062<li>

4063<a href="#_TrialSearch_502_sid_10_toc">

4064Current Clinical Trials</a>

4065</li>

4066</ul>

4067</a>

4068</li>

4069</ul>

4070</nav>

4071<p id="_45" tabindex="-1">

4072 Approximately 50% of relapses in patients with recurrent osteosarcoma occur within 18 months of therapy termination, and only 5% of recurrences develop beyond 5 years.[<a href="#cit/section_9.1">

40731</a>

4074-<a href="#cit/section_9.4">

40754</a>

4076] </p>

4077<section id="_1958">

4078<h3 id="_1958_toc">

4079Prognostic Factors for Recurrence</h3>

4080<p id="_1856" tabindex="-1">

4081Prognostic factors for recurrent osteosarcoma or undifferentiated pleomorphic sarcoma (UPS) of bone include the following:</p>

4082<div class="pdq-content-list">

4083<ul id="_1857">

4084<li>

4085<strong>

4086Time from diagnosis.</strong>

4087 In 564 patients with a recurrence, patients whose disease recurred within 2 years of diagnosis had a worse prognosis than patients whose disease recurred after 2 years.[<a href="#cit/section_9.1">

40881</a>

4089] In another series of 431 patients, recurrences occurring less than 2 years from diagnosis were also associated with worse outcomes.[<a href="#cit/section_9.5">

40905</a>

4091]</li>

4092<li>

4093<strong>

4094Age at initial diagnosis.</strong>

4095 Older age at initial study enrollment was associated with a worse prognosis.[<a href="#cit/section_9.5">

40965</a>

4097]</li>

4098<li>

4099<strong>

4100Presence of metastatic disease at diagnosis.</strong>

4101 The presence of metastatic disease at initial presentation was associated with a worse prognosis.[<a href="#cit/section_9.5">

41025</a>

4103]</li>

4104<li>

4105<strong>

4106Tumor response to preoperative chemotherapy.</strong>

4107 Patients with a good histologic response to initial preoperative chemotherapy had a better overall survival (OS) after recurrence than did poor initial responders.[<a href="#cit/section_9.1">

41081</a>

4109]</li>

4110<li>

4111<strong>

4112Site of metastases.</strong>

4113 The probability of developing lung metastases at 5 years is 28% in patients presenting with localized disease.[<a href="#cit/section_9.6">

41146</a>

4115] In two large series, the incidence of recurrence by site was as follows: lung only (65%&#8211;80%), bone only (8%&#8211;10%), local recurrence only (4%&#8211;7%), and combined relapse (10%&#8211;15%).[<a href="#cit/section_9.4">

41164</a>

4117,<a href="#cit/section_9.7">

41187</a>

4119] Abdominal metastases are rare but may occur as late as 4 years after diagnosis.[<a href="#cit/section_9.8">

41208</a>

4121] The Children's Oncology Group (COG) reported the outcomes of 431 young patients with recurrent osteosarcoma.[<a href="#cit/section_9.5">

41225</a>

4123][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4124Level of evidence C3</a>

4125] Patients with recurrences in both lung and bone had worse outcomes than did patients with recurrences in lung only (<em>

4126P</em>

4127 = .005).</li>

4128<li>

4129<strong>

4130Surgical resectability.</strong>

4131 Patients with recurrent

4132osteosarcoma should be assessed for surgical

4133resectability because they may sometimes be cured with aggressive surgical

4134resection with or without chemotherapy.[<a href="#cit/section_9.9">

41359</a>

4136,<a href="#cit/section_9.7">

41377</a>

4138,<a href="#cit/section_9.10">

413910</a>

4140-<a href="#cit/section_9.13">

414113</a>

4142] <p id="_1858" tabindex="-1">

4143Control of osteosarcoma after recurrence depends on complete surgical resection of all sites of clinically detectable metastatic disease. If surgical resection is not attempted or cannot be performed, progression and death are certain. The ability to achieve a complete

4144resection of recurrent disease is the most important prognostic factor at first

4145relapse, with a 5-year survival rate of 20% to 45% after complete

4146resection of metastatic pulmonary tumors and a 20% survival rate after complete resection of metastases at other sites.[<a href="#cit/section_9.4">

41474</a>

4148,<a href="#cit/section_9.7">

41497</a>

4150,<a href="#cit/section_9.13">

415113</a>

4152,<a href="#cit/section_9.14">

415314</a>

4154]</p>

4155</li>

4156</ul>

4157</div>

4158</section>

4159<section id="_1890">

4160<h3 id="_1890_toc">

4161Treatment Options for Recurrent Osteosarcoma and UPS of Bone</h3>

4162<p id="_1859" tabindex="-1">

4163Treatment options for patients with recurrent osteosarcoma or UPS of bone include the following:</p>

4164<div class="pdq-content-list">

4165<ol id="_1860">

4166<li>

4167<a href="/types/bone/hp/osteosarcoma-treatment-pdq#_1943">

4168Surgery</a>

4169 to remove all sites of metastatic disease.</li>

4170<li>

4171<a href="/types/bone/hp/osteosarcoma-treatment-pdq#_1945">

4172Chemotherapy and targeted therapy</a>

4173.</li>

4174<li>

4175<a href="/types/bone/hp/osteosarcoma-treatment-pdq#_1946">

4176Radiopharmaceuticals and radiation therapy</a>

4177.</li>

4178</ol>

4179</div>

4180<section id="_1943">

4181<h4 id="_1943_toc">

4182Surgery</h4>

4183<p id="_1944" tabindex="-1">

4184Control of osteosarcoma after recurrence depends on complete surgical resection of all sites of clinically detectable metastatic disease. A multi-institutional retrospective analysis compared thoracotomy with thoracoscopy for resection of pulmonary metastases in patients with osteosarcoma.[<a href="#cit/section_9.15">

418515</a>

4186] The analysis included patients who had pulmonary metastases at diagnosis, patients with pulmonary relapse after initial management of localized disease, and patients with disease progression while on therapy. The authors recognized a significant selection bias for the patients chosen to undergo thoracoscopy. In a Cox regression analysis, controlling for other factors impacting outcome, there was a significantly increased risk of mortality (hazard ratio [HR], 2.11; 95% confidence interval [CI], 1.09&#8211;4.09; <em>

4187P</em>

4188 = .027) but not pulmonary recurrence (HR, 0.96; 95% CI, 0.52&#8211;1.79; <em>

4189P</em>

4190 = .90) with a thoracoscopic approach. In a subset analysis limited to patients with oligometastatic disease, thoracoscopy did not increase the risk of mortality (HR, 1.16; 95% CI, 0.64&#8211;2.11; <em>

4191P</em>

4192 = .62). The ongoing randomized trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT05235165">

4193AOST2031 [NCT05235165]</a>

4194) was designed to definitively address this question and the selection bias. This trial will compare the effect of thoracotomy with thoracoscopic surgery.</p>

4195</section>

4196<section id="_1945">

4197<h4 id="_1945_toc">

4198Chemotherapy and targeted therapy</h4>

4199<p id="_155" tabindex="-1">

4200The role of systemic chemotherapy for the treatment of patients with recurrent osteosarcoma is not well defined. The selection of further systemic treatment

4201depends on many factors, including the site of recurrence, the patient&#8217;s

4202previous primary treatment, and individual patient considerations.</p>

4203<p id="_1898" tabindex="-1">

4204The COG reported the outcomes of patients with recurrent osteosarcoma from seven phase II trials, all of which were assessed to have shown no treatment benefit.[<a href="#cit/section_9.16">

420516</a>

4206] </p>

4207<div class="pdq-content-list">

4208<ul id="_1979">

4209<li>

4210The event-free survival (EFS) rate for 96 patients with osteosarcoma and measurable disease was 12% at 4 months (95% CI, 6%&#8211;19%). </li>

4211<li>

4212There was no significant difference in EFS between the trials according to the number of previous treatment regimens or patient age, sex, and ethnicity.</li>

4213</ul>

4214</div>

4215<p id="_1980" tabindex="-1">

4216One additional phase II trial with a different study design was reported. In this trial, patients with osteosarcoma and metastases to the lung underwent surgical resection of all lung nodules and then were treated with adjuvant inhaled granulocyte-macrophage colony-stimulating factor (GM-CSF).[<a href="#cit/section_9.16">

421716</a>

4218]</p>

4219<div class="pdq-content-list">

4220<ul id="_1981">

4221<li>

4222The 12-month EFS rate for the 42 evaluable patients enrolled in this study was 20% (95% CI, 10%&#8211;34%).</li>

4223</ul>

4224</div>

4225<p id="_1861" tabindex="-1">

4226The following chemotherapy and targeted therapy agents have been studied to treat recurrent osteosarcoma and UPS of bone:</p>

4227<div class="pdq-content-list">

4228<ul id="_1862">

4229<li>

4230<strong>

4231Ifosfamide

4232alone with mesna uroprotection, or in combination with etoposide.</strong>

4233 Ifosfamide

4234alone with mesna uroprotection, or in combination with etoposide, has been active in as many as one-third of patients with recurrent osteosarcoma who have

4235not previously received this drug.[<a href="#cit/section_9.17">

423617</a>

4237-<a href="#cit/section_9.21">

423821</a>

4239]</li>

4240<li>

4241<strong>

4242Gemcitabine and docetaxel.</strong>

4243 A nonrandomized comparison of two doses of gemcitabine, both given with docetaxel, suggested that a higher dose of gemcitabine (900 mg/m<span class="sup">

42442</span>

4245) was associated with a better response rate and longer survival than was a lower dose of gemcitabine (675 mg/m<span class="sup">

42462</span>

4247) for recurrent or refractory osteosarcoma.[<a href="#cit/section_9.22">

424822</a>

4249][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4250Level of evidence C1</a>

4251] The combination of gemcitabine (at a dose of 900 mg/m<span class="sup">

42522</span>

4253) and docetaxel has also been reported to have activity in some studies that included patients with unresectable disease.[<a href="#cit/section_9.23">

425423</a>

4255-<a href="#cit/section_9.25">

425625</a>

4257]; [<a href="#cit/section_9.26">

425826</a>

4259][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4260Level of evidence C3</a>

4261]</li>

4262<li>

4263<strong>

4264Cyclophosphamide and etoposide.</strong>

4265 Cyclophosphamide and etoposide have been shown to have activity in recurrent osteosarcoma.[<a href="#cit/section_9.23">

426623</a>

4267]</li>

4268<li>

4269<strong>

4270Sorafenib.</strong>

4271 The Italian Sarcoma Group reported rare objective responses and disease stabilization with sorafenib in patients with recurrent osteosarcoma.[<a href="#cit/section_9.27">

427227</a>

4273]</li>

4274<li>

4275<strong>

4276Sorafenib and everolimus.</strong>

4277 The Italian Sarcoma Group also reported the outcome of patients with metastatic recurrent osteosarcoma treated with the combination of sorafenib and everolimus. They observed two partial responses and two minor responses in 38 patients; 17 of 38 patients were progression free at 6 months from study entry but toxicity was greater than with sorafenib monotherapy.[<a href="#cit/section_9.28">

427828</a>

4279][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4280Level of evidence B4</a>

4281]</li>

4282<li>

4283<strong>

4284Regorafenib.</strong>

4285 Two prospective, randomized, double-blind trials have evaluated the role of regorafenib in the treatment of metastatic recurrent osteosarcoma. Both studies used the approved treatment regimen of 160 mg by mouth daily for 21 days followed by 7 days without treatment. The French trial randomly assigned patients 2:1 between regorafenib and placebo and allowed crossover for patients assigned to placebo.[<a href="#cit/section_9.29">

428629</a>

4287] Seventeen of 26 patients (65%; one-sided 95% CI, 47%) in the regorafenib group did not have disease progression at 8 weeks, compared with 0 of 12 patients in the placebo group. The Sarcoma Alliance for Research Collaboration (SARC) group randomly assigned adult patients 1:1 between regorafenib and placebo.[<a href="#cit/section_9.30">

428830</a>

4289] Median progression-free survival (PFS) was significantly improved with regorafenib versus placebo: 3.6 months (95% CI, 2.0&#8211;7.6 months) versus 1.7 months (95% CI, 1.2&#8211;1.8 months), respectively (HR, 0.42; 95% CI, 0.21&#8211;0.85; <em>

4290P</em>

4291 = .017).</li>

4292<li>

4293<strong>

4294Dinutuximab in combination with GM-CSF.</strong>

4295 The COG performed a phase II study of dinutuximab, an antidisialoganglioside antibody, in combination with GM-CSF for patients with recurrent osteosarcoma. Of 39 patients, 28 experienced an event, and only 28.2% (95% CI, 15%&#8211;44.9%) of patients were event-free at the 12-month benchmark. Dinutuximab did not demonstrate sufficient evidence of efficacy.[<a href="#cit/section_9.31">

429631</a>

4297]</li>

4298<li>

4299<strong>

4300Denosumab.</strong>

4301 The COG performed a phase II study of denosumab, a fully human monoclonal antibody to the receptor activator of nuclear factor-kappa beta ligand (RANKL). Patients aged 11 to 49 years with recurrent osteosarcoma were eligible for the study. Patients with measurable disease were eligible for cohort 1, and patients who underwent complete surgical resection of all sites of recurrent disease were eligible for cohort 2. The event-free rate did not exceed the historical rate experienced in previous COG trials to meet the study defined efficacy criteria in either cohort.[<a href="#cit/section_9.32">

430232</a>

4303]</li>

4304<li>

4305<strong>

4306Lenvatinib with ifosfamide and etoposide.</strong>

4307 A multi-institutional group performed a phase I/II study using a combination of lenvatinib, ifosfamide, and etoposide to treat patients with relapsed or refractory osteosarcoma.[<a href="#cit/section_9.33">

430833</a>

4309][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4310Level of evidence B4</a>

4311] The study suggested phase II doses for each drug: 1) 14 mg/m<span class="sup">

43122</span>

4313 per day of lenvatinib (with a daily dose cap of 24 mg), 2) 100 mg/m<span class="sup">

43142</span>

4315 per day of etoposide, and 3) 3,000 mg/m<span class="sup">

43162</span>

4317 per day of ifosfamide. These drugs were given to patients intravenously on days 1 to 3 of each 3-week cycle for five cycles at most. Thirty-five patients from the phase I (cohort 3A; n = 15) and phase II (cohort 3B; n = 20) trials were treated at the recommended phase II doses, and their results were pooled. Eighteen of 35 patients had PFS rates of 51% (95% CI, 34%&#8211;69%) after 4 months, per the binomial estimate.</li>

4318</ul>

4319</div>

4320</section>

4321<section id="_1946">

4322<h4 id="_1946_toc">

4323Radiopharmaceuticals and radiation therapy</h4>

4324<p id="_1864" tabindex="-1">

4325High-dose samarium Sm 153-ethylenediamine tetramethylene phosphonic acid (153Sm-EDTMP) coupled with peripheral blood stem

4326cell support may provide significant pain palliation in patients with bone

4327metastases.[<a href="#cit/section_9.34">

432834</a>

4329-<a href="#cit/section_9.37">

433037</a>

4331] Toxicity of 153Sm-EDTMP is primarily hematologic.[<a href="#cit/section_9.38">

433238</a>

4333][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4334Level of evidence C2</a>

4335]</p>

4336<p id="_1915" tabindex="-1">

4337A single-institution retrospective review reported that high-dose fraction radiation therapy (2 Gy/fraction) was a useful form of palliation for patients with recurrent osteosarcoma.[<a href="#cit/section_9.39">

433839</a>

4339][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4340Level of evidence C3</a>

4341] Thirty-two courses of palliative radiation therapy were given to 20 patients with symptomatic metastatic and/or locally recurrent primary disease. Twenty-four of the 32 courses (75%) were associated with symptom improvement. Higher doses of radiation therapy correlated with longer durations of symptom response.</p>

4342</section>

4343</section>

4344<section id="_275">

4345<h3 id="_275_toc">

4346Treatment Options for Local Recurrence</h3>

4347<p id="_1959" tabindex="-1">

4348Treatment options for patients with osteosarcoma or UPS of bone that has recurred locally include the following:</p>

4349<div class="pdq-content-list">

4350<ol id="_1960">

4351<li>

4352Surgery to remove the tumor.</li>

4353</ol>

4354</div>

4355<p id="_276" tabindex="-1">

4356 The postrelapse outcome of

4357patients who have a local recurrence is quite poor,[<a href="#cit/section_9.40">

435840</a>

4359-<a href="#cit/section_9.42">

436042</a>

4361] and survival of patients with local recurrences and either previous or concurrent systemic metastases is poor.[<a href="#cit/section_9.43">

436243</a>

4363]</p>

4364<p id="_1961" tabindex="-1">

4365Two retrospective, single-institution series reported a survival rate of 10% to 40% after local recurrence without associated systemic metastasis.[<a href="#cit/section_9.43">

436643</a>

4367-<a href="#cit/section_9.46">

436846</a>

4369]</p>

4370<p id="_1962" tabindex="-1">

4371 A retrospective review from the Italian Sarcoma Group identified 62 patients (median age, 21 years) with local recurrences.[<a href="#cit/section_9.47">

437247</a>

4373] With a median follow-up of 43 months (range, 5&#8211;235 months), the 5-year post&#8211;local relapse survival rate was 37%, significantly better for patients with a longer local recurrence&#8211;free interval (&#8804;24 months, 31% vs. &gt;24 months, 61.5%; <em>

4374P</em>

4375 = .03), absence of distant metastases (no distant metastases, 56% vs. distant metastases, 11.5%; <em>

4376P</em>

4377 = .0001), and achievement of second complete remission (CR2) by surgical resection (no CR2, 0% vs. CR2, 58.5%; <em>

4378P</em>

4379 = .0001). No difference in post&#8211;local relapse survival was found according to age, and there was no benefit from chemotherapy administration.</p>

4380<p id="_1876" tabindex="-1">

4381The incidence of local relapse was higher

4382in patients who had a poor pathologic response to

4383chemotherapy in the primary tumor and in patients with inadequate surgical margins.[<a href="#cit/section_9.40">

438440</a>

4385,<a href="#cit/section_9.45">

438645</a>

4387]</p>

4388</section>

4389<section id="_271">

4390<h3 id="_271_toc">

4391Treatment Options for Lung-Only Recurrence</h3>

4392<p id="_1963" tabindex="-1">

4393Treatment options for patients with osteosarcoma and UPS of bone that has recurred in the lung only include the following:</p>

4394<div class="pdq-content-list">

4395<ol id="_1964">

4396<li>

4397Surgery to remove the tumor.</li>

4398<li>

4399Targeted therapy (sorafenib and regorafenib).</li>

4400</ol>

4401</div>

4402<p id="_272" tabindex="-1">

4403Repeated resections of pulmonary recurrences can lead to extended disease control and possibly cure for some patients.[<a href="#cit/section_9.14">

440414</a>

4405,<a href="#cit/section_9.48">

440648</a>

4407] Survival for patients with unresectable metastatic disease is less than 5%.[<a href="#cit/section_9.7">

44087</a>

4409,<a href="#cit/section_9.49">

441049</a>

4411] The 5-year EFS rate for patients who have complete surgical resection of all pulmonary metastases ranges from 20% to 45%.[<a href="#cit/section_9.4">

44124</a>

4413,<a href="#cit/section_9.13">

441413</a>

4415,<a href="#cit/section_9.14">

441614</a>

4417]; [<a href="#cit/section_9.50">

441850</a>

4419][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4420Level of evidence C1</a>

4421]</p>

4422<p id="_1865" tabindex="-1">

4423Factors associated with a

4424better outcome include the following:[<a href="#cit/section_9.4">

44254</a>

4426,<a href="#cit/section_9.6">

44276</a>

4428,<a href="#cit/section_9.7">

44297</a>

4430,<a href="#cit/section_9.51">

443151</a>

4432,<a href="#cit/section_9.52">

443352</a>

4434] </p>

4435<div class="pdq-content-list">

4436<ul id="_1965">

4437<li>

4438 Fewer pulmonary nodules.</li>

4439<li>

4440Unilateral pulmonary

4441metastases.</li>

4442<li>

4443Longer intervals between primary tumor resection and

4444metastases.</li>

4445<li>

4446Tumor location in the periphery of the lung.</li>

4447</ul>

4448</div>

4449<p id="_1966" tabindex="-1">

4450Approximately 50% of patients with one isolated pulmonary lesion more than 1 year after diagnosis were long-term survivors after metastasectomy. Chemotherapy did not appear to offer an advantage.[<a href="#cit/section_9.53">

445153</a>

4452][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4453Level of evidence C1</a>

4454]</p>

4455<p id="_455" tabindex="-1">

4456Control of osteosarcoma requires surgical resection of all macroscopic tumors; however, recommendations are conflicting regarding the surgical approach to the treatment of pulmonary metastases in osteosarcoma. Several options are available to resect pulmonary nodules in a patient with osteosarcoma, including thoracoscopy and thoracotomy with palpation of the collapsed lung. When patients have nodules identified only in one lung, some surgeons advocate thoracoscopy, some advocate unilateral thoracotomy, and some advocate bilateral thoracotomy. Bilateral thoracotomy can be performed as a single surgical procedure with a median sternotomy or a clamshell approach, or by staged bilateral thoracotomies.</p>

4457<p id="_1869" tabindex="-1">

4458Evidence (surgical approach for lung-only recurrence of osteosarcoma and UPS of bone):</p>

4459<div class="pdq-content-list">

4460<ol id="_1870">

4461<li>

4462The St. Jude Children&#8217;s Research Hospital reported on 81 patients who had pulmonary nodules identified at initial presentation in only one lung by computed tomography (CT) scan.[<a href="#cit/section_9.54">

446354</a>

4464] They performed unilateral thoracotomy and did not explore the contralateral hemithorax. At the time of thoracotomy, 44 of 81 patients had a solitary nodule identified; 15 of 81 patients had two nodules identified; 16 of 81 patients had three to five nodules identified; and 6 of 81 patients had more than five nodules identified. Additional patients who were considered unresectable were not included in the analysis. <div class="pdq-content-list">

4465<ul id="_1871">

4466<li>

4467Thirty-nine of 81 patients had subsequent pulmonary recurrence; for most patients, recurrence occurred within 6 months.</li>

4468<li>

4469Within the first 6 months, 9 of 81 patients had ipsilateral recurrence, and 10 of 81 patients had a contralateral recurrence. By 2 years after initial thoracotomy, 13 of 81 patients had ipsilateral recurrence; 19 of 81 patients had contralateral recurrence; and 2 of 81 patients had bilateral recurrence.</li>

4470<li>

4471OS was similar for patients with ipsilateral and bilateral recurrence.</li>

4472</ul>

4473</div>

4474</li>

4475<li>

4476The Memorial Sloan Kettering Cancer Center reported on pulmonary metastatic disease recurrence after initial therapy for osteosarcoma. Fourteen patients had pulmonary nodules identified in only one lung by CT scan; nine patients were identified less than 2 years from initial diagnosis (early metastases), and five patients were identified more than 2 years from initial diagnosis (late metastases).[<a href="#cit/section_9.51">

447751</a>

4478] Seven of nine patients with early metastases had staged contralateral thoracotomies, and six of seven had nodules removed from the contralateral lung, despite negative CT scan findings. <div class="pdq-content-list">

4479<ul id="_1872">

4480<li>

4481The lack of a comparison group precludes evaluation of the impact of the contralateral thoracotomy on subsequent EFS or OS.</li>

4482<li>

4483The same group expanded their analysis to include a retrospective review of 161 thoracotomies performed in 88 patients with osteosarcoma metastatic to the lung.[<a href="#cit/section_9.55">

448455</a>

4485] In this expanded series, CT failed to identify one-third of pulmonary metastases confirmed by pathological examination.</li>

4486</ul>

4487</div>

4488</li>

4489</ol>

4490</div>

4491</section>

4492<section id="_273">

4493<h3 id="_273_toc">

4494Treatment Options for Recurrence With Bone-Only Metastases</h3>

4495<p id="_1873" tabindex="-1">

4496Treatment options for patients with osteosarcoma or UPS of bone that has recurred in the bone only include the following:</p>

4497<div class="pdq-content-list">

4498<ol id="_1874">

4499<li>

4500Surgery to remove the tumor.</li>

4501<li>

4502153Sm-EDTMP with or without stem cell support.</li>

4503<li>

4504Targeted therapy (sorafenib and regorafenib).</li>

4505<li>

4506Radiation therapy.</li>

4507</ol>

4508</div>

4509<p id="_274" tabindex="-1">

4510Patients with osteosarcoma who develop bone metastases have a poor prognosis. In one large series, the 5-year EFS rate was 11%.[<a href="#cit/section_9.56">

451156</a>

4512] Patients with late solitary bone relapse have a 5-year EFS rate of approximately 30%.[<a href="#cit/section_9.56">

451356</a>

4514-<a href="#cit/section_9.59">

451559</a>

4516]</p>

4517<p id="_1875" tabindex="-1">

4518For patients with multiple unresectable bone lesions, 153Sm-EDTMP with or without stem cell support may produce stable disease and/or provide pain relief.[<a href="#cit/section_9.38">

451938</a>

4520]</p>

4521<p id="_2399" tabindex="-1">

4522External-beam radiation therapy can provide local control of recurrent unresectable disease, symptomatic, and/or metastatic disease. Radiation therapy techniques allow for the delivery of very conformal high doses, known as stereotactic ablative radiation therapy (SABR) or stereotactic body radiation therapy (SBRT). SBRT and SABR administer treatment with high conformality and precision over a short period of time, providing good palliation and local control.[<a href="#cit/section_9.60">

452360</a>

4524]</p>

4525</section>

4526<section id="_278">

4527<h3 id="_278_toc">

4528Treatment Options for Second Recurrence of Osteosarcoma</h3>

4529<p id="_1877" tabindex="-1">

4530Treatment options for patients with osteosarcoma or UPS of bone that has recurred twice include the following:</p>

4531<div class="pdq-content-list">

4532<ol id="_1878">

4533<li>

4534Surgery to remove the tumor and/or chemotherapy.</li>

4535<li>

4536Targeted therapy (sorafenib and regorafenib).</li>

4537</ol>

4538</div>

4539<p id="_1967" tabindex="-1">

4540Evidence (surgery and/or chemotherapy):</p>

4541<div class="pdq-content-list">

4542<ol id="_1968">

4543<li>

4544The cooperative German-Austrian-Swiss osteosarcoma study group reported on 249 patients who had a second recurrence of osteosarcoma. The main feature of therapy was repeated surgical resection of recurrent disease.[<a href="#cit/section_9.61">

454561</a>

4546]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4547<ul id="_1969">

4548<li>

4549 Of these patients, 197 died and 37 were alive in CR (24 patients after a third complete response and 13 patients after a fourth or subsequent complete response).</li>

4550<li>

4551 Fifteen patients who did not achieve surgical remission remained alive, but follow-up for these patients was extremely short.</li>

4552</ul>

4553</div>

4554</li>

4555<li>

4556The Spanish Group for Research on Sarcoma reported the results of a phase II trial of patients with relapsed or refractory osteosarcoma who were treated with gemcitabine and sirolimus.[<a href="#cit/section_9.62">

455762</a>

4558][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4559Level of evidence C3</a>

4560] <div class="pdq-content-list">

4561<ul id="_1970">

4562<li>

4563The PFS rate at 4&#8201;months was 44%. </li>

4564<li>

4565After central radiologic review of 33 assessable patients, 2 partial responses and 14 disease stabilizations (48.5%) were reported.</li>

4566</ul>

4567</div>

4568</li>

4569<li>

4570 The COG reported the outcomes of patients with recurrent osteosarcoma from seven phase II trials, all of which were assessed to have shown no treatment benefit.[<a href="#cit/section_9.16">

457116</a>

4572]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4573<ul id="_1971">

4574<li>

4575 The EFS rate for 96 patients with osteosarcoma and measurable disease was 12% at 4 months (95% CI, 6%&#8211;19%).</li>

4576<li>

4577 There was no significant difference in EFS between the trials according to the number of previous treatment regimens or patient age, sex, and ethnicity. </li>

4578</ul>

4579</div>

4580</li>

4581<li>

4582One additional phase II trial with a different study design was reported. In this trial, patients with osteosarcoma and metastases to the lung underwent surgical resection of all lung nodules and then were treated with adjuvant inhaled GM-CSF.[<a href="#cit/section_9.16">

458316</a>

4584]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4585<ul id="_1972">

4586<li>

4587 The 12-month EFS rate for the 42 evaluable patients enrolled in this study was 20% (95% CI, 10%&#8211;34%).</li>

4588</ul>

4589</div>

4590</li>

4591</ol>

4592</div>

4593</section>

4594<section id="_502">

4595<h3 id="_502_toc">

4596Treatment Options Under Clinical Evaluation</h3>

4597<p id="_2414" tabindex="-1">

4598Information about National Cancer Institute (NCI)&#8211;supported clinical trials can be found on the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search">

4599NCI website</a>

4600. For information about clinical trials sponsored by other organizations, see the <a href="https://clinicaltrials.gov/" title="https://clinicaltrials.gov/">

4601ClinicalTrials.gov website</a>

4602.</p>

4603<p id="_2415" tabindex="-1">

4604The following are examples of national and/or institutional clinical trials that are currently being conducted:</p>

4605<div class="pdq-content-list">

4606<ul id="_504">

4607<li>

4608<strong>

4609<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT03155620">

4610APEC1621 (NCT03155620)</a>

4611</strong>

4612 (Pediatric MATCH: Targeted Therapy Directed by Genetic Testing in Treating Pediatric Patients with Relapsed or Refractory Advanced Solid Tumors, Non-Hodgkin Lymphomas, or Histiocytic Disorders)<strong>

4613:</strong>

4614 NCI-COG Pediatric Molecular Analysis for Therapeutic Choice (MATCH), referred to as Pediatric MATCH, will match targeted agents with specific molecular changes identified in a patient's tumor (refractory or recurrent). Children and adolescents aged 1 to 21 years are eligible for the trial.<p id="_1807" tabindex="-1">

4615Patients with tumors that have molecular variants addressed by open treatment arms in the trial may be enrolled in treatment on Pediatric MATCH. Additional information can be obtained on the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/nci-supported/pediatric-match" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/nci-supported/pediatric-match">

4616NCI website</a>

4617 and <a href="https://clinicaltrials.gov/ct2/show/NCT03155620" title="https://clinicaltrials.gov/ct2/show/NCT03155620">

4618ClinicalTrials.gov website</a>

4619.</p>

4620

4621</li>

4622<li>

4623<strong>

4624<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT04539366">

4625GD2-CAR PERSIST (NCT04539366)</a>

4626</strong>

4627 (Testing a New Immune Cell Therapy, GD2-Targeted Modified T-cells (GD2CART), in Children, Adolescents, and Young Adults with Relapsed/Refractory Osteosarcoma and Neuroblastoma)<strong>

4628:</strong>

4629 This is a phase I trial to determine the side effects and best dose of GD2CART to be effective against GD2-positive tumor cells.</li>

4630</ul>

4631</div>

4632<section id="_TrialSearch_502_sid_10">

4633<h4 id="_TrialSearch_502_sid_10_toc">

4634Current Clinical Trials</h4>

4635<p id="_TrialSearch_502_22" tabindex="-1">

4636Use our <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced">

4637advanced clinical trial search</a>

4638 to find NCI-supported cancer clinical trials that are now enrolling patients. The search can be narrowed by location of the trial, type of treatment, name of the drug, and other criteria. <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/">

4639General information</a>

4640 about clinical trials is also available.</p>

4901 <section id="_65">

4902

4903 <h2>

4904Changes to This Summary (04/05/2023)</h2>

4905

4906 <div id="_section_65" class="pdq-sections">

4907<p id="_70" tabindex="-1">

4908The PDQ cancer information summaries are reviewed regularly and updated as

4909new information becomes available. This section describes the latest

4910changes made to this summary as of the date above.</p>

4911<p id="_2422" tabindex="-1">

4912<strong>

4913<a href="/types/bone/hp/osteosarcoma-treatment-pdq#_38">

4914Treatment of Osteosarcoma and Undifferentiated Pleomorphic Sarcoma (UPS) of Bone With Metastatic Disease at Diagnosis</a>

4915</strong>

4916</p>

4917<p id="_2423" tabindex="-1">

4918Added <a href="/types/bone/hp/osteosarcoma-treatment-pdq#_2403">

4919AOST2032</a>

4920 as a clinical trial that is currently available for patients with newly diagnosed localized and metastatic osteosarcoma.</p>

4921<p id="_2421" tabindex="-1">

4922<strong>

4923<a href="/types/bone/hp/osteosarcoma-treatment-pdq#_44">

4924Treatment of Recurrent Osteosarcoma and UPS of Bone</a>

4925</strong>

4926</p>

4927<p id="_2424" tabindex="-1">

4928Added <a href="/types/bone/hp/osteosarcoma-treatment-pdq#_1862">

4929dinutuximab in combination with GM-CSF</a>

4930 as a regimen that has been studied to treat recurrent osteosarcoma and UPS of bone. Also added text to state that the Children's Oncology Group (COG) performed a phase II study of dinutuximab, an antidisialoganglioside antibody, in combination with GM-CSF for patients with recurrent osteosarcoma. Of 39 patients, 28 experienced an event, and only 28.2% of patients were event-free at the 12-month benchmark. Dinutuximab did not demonstrate sufficient evidence of efficacy (cited Hingorani et al. as reference 31).</p>

4931<p id="_2425" tabindex="-1">

4932Added <a href="/types/bone/hp/osteosarcoma-treatment-pdq#_1862">

4933denosumab</a>

4934 as a targeted therapy agent that has been studied to treat recurrent osteosarcoma and UPS of bone. Also added text to state that the COG performed a phase II study of denosumab, a fully human monoclonal antibody to the receptor activator of nuclear factor-kappa beta ligand. Patients aged 11 to 49 years with recurrent osteosarcoma were eligible for the study. Patients with measurable disease were eligible for cohort 1, and patients who underwent complete surgical resection of all sites of recurrent disease were eligible for cohort 2. The event-free rate did not exceed the historical rate experienced in previous COG trials to meet the study defined efficacy criteria in either cohort (cited Janeway et al. as reference 32).</p>

4935<p id="_disclaimerHP_3" tabindex="-1">

4936This summary is written and maintained by the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/pediatric-treatment" title="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/pediatric-treatment">

4937PDQ Pediatric Treatment Editorial Board</a>

4938, which is

4939editorially independent of NCI. The summary reflects an independent review of

4940the literature and does not represent a policy statement of NCI or NIH. More

4941information about summary policies and the role of the PDQ Editorial Boards in

4942maintaining the PDQ summaries can be found on the <a href="/types/bone/hp/osteosarcoma-treatment-pdq#_AboutThis_1">

4943About This PDQ Summary</a>

4944 and <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq" title="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq">

4945PDQ&#174; Cancer Information for Health Professionals</a>

4946 pages.

4947</p>

4948</div>

4954 <section id="_AboutThis_1">

4955

4956 <h2>

4957About This PDQ Summary</h2>

4958

4959 <div id="_section_AboutThis_1" class="pdq-sections">

4960<section id="_AboutThis_2">

4961<h3 id="_AboutThis_2_toc">

4962Purpose of This Summary</h3>

4963<p id="_AboutThis_3" tabindex="-1">

4964This PDQ cancer information summary for health professionals provides comprehensive, peer-reviewed, evidence-based information about the treatment of osteosarcoma and undifferentiated pleomorphic sarcoma of bone. It is intended as a resource to inform and assist clinicians in the care of their patients. It does not provide formal guidelines or recommendations for making health care decisions.</p>

4965</section>

4966<section id="_AboutThis_4">

4967<h3 id="_AboutThis_4_toc">

4968Reviewers and Updates</h3>

4969<p id="_AboutThis_5" tabindex="-1">

4970This summary is reviewed regularly and updated as necessary by the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/pediatric-treatment" title="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/pediatric-treatment">

4971PDQ Pediatric Treatment Editorial Board</a>

4972, which is editorially independent of the National Cancer Institute (NCI). The summary reflects an independent review of the literature and does not represent a policy statement of NCI or the National Institutes of Health (NIH).</p>

4973<p id="_AboutThis_22" tabindex="-1">

4974 Board members review recently published articles each month to determine whether an article should:</p>

4975<div class="pdq-content-list">

4976<ul id="_AboutThis_6">

4977<li>

4978be discussed at a meeting,</li>

4979<li>

4980be cited with text, or</li>

4981<li>

4982replace or update an existing article that is already cited.</li>

4983</ul>

4984</div>

4985<p id="_AboutThis_7" tabindex="-1">

4986Changes to the summaries are made through a consensus process in which Board members evaluate the strength of the evidence in the published articles and determine how the article should be included in the summary.</p>

4987<p id="" tabindex="-1">

4988The lead reviewers for Osteosarcoma and Undifferentiated Pleomorphic Sarcoma of Bone Treatment are:</p>

4989<div class="pdq-content-list">

4990<ul id="">

4991<li>

4992Holcombe Edwin Grier, MD</li>

4993<li>

4994Karen J. Marcus, MD, FACR (Dana-Farber Cancer Institute/Boston Children's Hospital)</li>

4995<li>

4996William H. Meyer, MD</li>

4997<li>

4998Paul A. Meyers, MD (Memorial Sloan-Kettering Cancer Center)</li>

4999<li>

5000Thomas A. Olson, MD (Aflac Cancer and Blood Disorders Center of Children's Healthcare of Atlanta - Egleston Campus)</li>

5001<li>

5002Nita Louise Seibel, MD (National Cancer Institute)</li>

5003<li>

5004Malcolm A. Smith, MD, PhD (National Cancer Institute)</li>

5005</ul>

5006</div>

5007<p id="_AboutThis_9" tabindex="-1">

5008Any comments or questions about the summary content should be submitted to Cancer.gov through the NCI website's <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/contact/email-us" title="https://www.cancer.gov/contact/email-us">

5009Email Us</a>

5010. Do not contact the individual Board Members with questions or comments about the summaries. Board members will not respond to individual inquiries.</p>

5011</section>

5012<section id="_AboutThis_10">

5013<h3 id="_AboutThis_10_toc">

5014Levels of Evidence</h3>

5015<p id="_AboutThis_11" tabindex="-1">

5016Some of the reference citations in this summary are accompanied by a level-of-evidence designation. These designations are intended to help readers assess the strength of the evidence supporting the use of specific interventions or approaches. The PDQ Pediatric Treatment Editorial Board uses a <a href="/publications/pdq/levels-evidence/treatment">

5017formal evidence ranking system</a>

5018 in developing its level-of-evidence designations.</p>

5019</section>

5020<section id="_AboutThis_12">

5021<h3 id="_AboutThis_12_toc">

5022Permission to Use This Summary</h3>

5023<p id="_AboutThis_13" tabindex="-1">

5024PDQ is a registered trademark. Although the content of PDQ documents can be used freely as text, it cannot be identified as an NCI PDQ cancer information summary unless it is presented in its entirety and is regularly updated. However, an author would be permitted to write a sentence such as &#8220;NCI&#8217;s PDQ cancer information summary about breast cancer prevention states the risks succinctly: [include excerpt from the summary].&#8221;</p>

5025<p id="_AboutThis_14" tabindex="-1">

5027<p id="_AboutThis_15" tabindex="-1">
